| v6.4.1 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 7 v2 hotfix: modal z-index** — v6.4.0 shipped with `_open3DPopup()` building the modal DOM correctly (`role="dialog"`, `aria-modal`, `display:flex`, `opacity:1`, fixed positioning at `inset:0`), but users clicking the 3D pill saw nothing happen. Root cause: the modal carried `z-index: 70`, while the TB v3 builder host wrapper uses `z-index: 100` and creates a stacking context. With both at `document.body` level but the builder's stacking context higher, the modal painted **behind** the builder chrome — fully constructed, fully styled, but invisible. Diagnostic confirmed: `modalInDom:true`, `isOpenClass:true`, `cardRect:{x:60, y:34, w:1320, h:832}`, `bodyOverflow:hidden` — all correct state, but a fresh Playwright screenshot showed the canvas with zero modal overlay. **Fix**: single CSS line — `.tb3-3d-popup-modal { z-index: 10001 }` (matches the app convention for top-level overlays: pro-only modal, quota-exceeded modal, and update-available toast all use the 9000–10000 range; modal needs to be above). `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r12 → r13` to cache-bust the stale CSS for users who already loaded v6.4.0. The v2 Stage 2 UAT guard locked the old `z-index: 70` value — migrated to lock the new `z-index: 10001`. UAT 6779/6779 still passes. **Known follow-up** (not in this hotfix): with the popup now visible, the 3D scene centroid is in the bottom-right corner of the viewport rather than centered — devices at positive canvas (x,y) translate outward from the stage origin at `left:50% top:50%`. Fix in next iteration is a centroid-offset on `_build3DDeviceEl` + `_build3DCableEl` so the topology renders centered regardless of its canvas coordinates. The popup is now visible and interactive; the centroid issue is cosmetic. |
| v6.4.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 7 v2: 3D popup** — the seventh phase on the v5.7.0 / v5.8.0/5.9.0 / v6.0.0 / v6.1.0 / v6.2.0 / v6.3.0 foundation. Where Phase 6 OSI mode annotates each hop with the full L1-L7 layer stack, Phase 7 v2 lifts the topology out of the flat canvas into a **3D modal lightbox** — a CSS-perspective viewport showing each device as an extruded bronze card, drag-to-rotate with momentum decay, scroll-to-zoom, double-click camera reset, and live sync with the canvas. **Architecture** (additive to the existing `features/topology-builder-v3.js` IIFE, ~+450 LOC JS + ~+140 LOC CSS vs Phase 6; no new feature modules; `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r11 → r12` at Stage 0): (1) **Modal lightbox, NOT a mode** — `state.mode` is not modified; the 3D popup is entirely transient. A module-scope `_3dPopup` object carries all ephemeral state: `{open, camera{rotX, rotY, zoom}, dragState, velocityX, velocityY, rafHandle}`. The modal DOM is built fresh on `_open3DPopup()` and removed on `_close3DPopup()` — zero durable state, zero localStorage writes. (2) **Three close paths** — X button, Esc key, backdrop click. All call `_close3DPopup()` which cancels the rAF handle, removes the modal DOM, and restores the 3D modebar pill to its default state. Focus trap on open (focus returns to the pill on close). (3) **CSS 3D only** — no Three.js / WebGL. Each device renders as a `perspective`-transformed `<div>` with a top face (icon + label), four side rims, and a bottom face via CSS `rotateX` + `translateZ`. The floor has a radial vignette. Scene rotation is driven entirely by CSS `transform: rotateX(${rotX}deg) rotateY(${rotY}deg) scale(${zoom})` on the stage element. (4) **Render-copy architecture** — `_render3DScene` builds a parallel DOM mirror from `state.devices` and `state.cables`; the main `#tb3-canvas-svg` is never touched. (5) **Live sync** — a single tail-call in `_renderCanvas` (line ~2020): `if (_3dPopup.open) _render3DScene();`. Any canvas state mutation that calls `_renderCanvas` automatically keeps the 3D scene in sync without a separate subscription. (6) **Motion engine** — drag events drive `_3dPopup.velocityX`/`velocityY` accumulation; on mouseup a `requestAnimationFrame` momentum loop applies Emil-tuned 0.92/0.94 decay per frame until velocity falls below 0.05 deg/frame. Vertical pitch is clamped 15°–75°. Scroll wheel applies a zoom delta clamped 0.4×–3.0×. Double-click runs a 320–400ms linear tween back to the default camera (`rotX 30°, rotY −20°, zoom 1.0`) via rAF. All motion cancels on popup close. (7) **Reduced-motion fallback** — `matchMedia('(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)')` gates the CSS entry animation (instant open, no fade-in/scale) and disables the momentum decay loop (scene stops on mouseup immediately). Drag rotation remains active (input-driven, not CSS animation). (8) **Scoped CSS** — all rules under `.tb3-3d-popup-*` class / `#tb3-3d-popup-*` id prefix; zero bleed to the main canvas or other pages. (9) **Stop-slop copy validation** (via `stop-slop` skill, all 5 templates clean): modal title `"3D view of topology"` — specific, no filler; counts line `"{N} devices · {M} cables"` — middle-dot separator, no em-dash; empty state `"Add devices to the canvas to see them in 3D."` — active imperative, no weasel words; X button aria-label `"Close 3D view"` — direct; viewport aria-label `"3D rendering of {N} devices and {M} cables. Use arrow keys to rotate, plus or minus to zoom, R to reset, Escape to close."` — complete, no redundancy. All 5 passed the stop-slop rubric with no suggested tightenings. **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+~450 LOC: `_3dPopup` module-scope state + `_open3DPopup` + `_close3DPopup` + `_render3DScene` + drag/velocity/rAF motion handlers + scroll zoom + double-click tween + live-sync tail-call in `_renderCanvas` + focus trap + Esc handler + reduced-motion gate + registration object exposures `_open3DPopup`/`_close3DPopup`); `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+~140 LOC scoped Phase 7 v2 block: modal overlay + backdrop blur + header + counts line + viewport + CSS 3D stage + device card faces + floor vignette + entry animation + `@media prefers-reduced-motion` gate); `tests/uat.js` (UAT guards for `_3dPopup` state schema + three close paths + live-sync tail-call + reduced-motion gate + stop-slop copy template assertions); `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (+5 Playwright tests 54-58: popup opens with `role=dialog` + focus; drag changes camera transform; Esc closes cleanly + mode unchanged; live sync — device added while popup open appears in 3D scene; reduced-motion skips entry animation); `dogfood/tb-v3-phase7-popup.html` (NEW — 8-step founder smoke test covering empty-canvas modal, extruded 3D cards, drag rotation, momentum decay, scroll zoom, double-click reset, live sync, Esc + reduced-motion; self-contained HTML, dark forged-bronze theme, pass/fail radio buttons + running tally); `styles.css` (header version comment bumped v6.3.0 → v6.4.0 via `bump-version.js` side-effect, included in a release follow-up commit). **Tests**: UAT **6779/6779** (was 6753 at v6.3.0 + new Phase 7 v2 UAT guards). Playwright **chromium 166/166** (was 161 at v6.3.0 + 5 new Phase 7 v2 tests 54-58, all passing: ✓54 313ms / ✓55 359ms / ✓56 329ms / ✓57 349ms / ✓58 346ms). Tech-debt clean (no new breaches; 2 pre-existing saas-gated breaches unchanged). **Process**: `stop-slop` skill copy validation (all 5 templates clean, no AI-tells or weasel words) → UAT guards → Playwright tests 54-58 → dogfood HTML (8 steps). **Phase 8+ deferred** (per founder direction): Phase 8 = Coach mode (Tier C AI tutor with reachability + Trace + OSI awareness, reads `_failedReasonToLayer` for layer-anchored explanations) · Phase 9 = Grade mode (PBQ-style scoring against Trace + OSI completion criteria) · Phase 10 = retire v1+v2 from sidebar + delete `features/topology-builder-v2` + delete v1 code from `app.js` (the strangler-fig payoff). **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (feature-module additive JS/CSS — no DB/auth/money/SW-fetch-logic; `sw.js` = universal CACHE_NAME bump from `bump-version.js`) → canonical trunk push, CI-gated. The Topology Builder v3 now ships its seventh phase: the 3D modebar pill (locked since Phase 1, phase-hinted "Coming soon") unlocks — students drag the canvas into perspective, watch device cards extrude, rotate the topology, and see the same live state the flat canvas shows. The `_3dPopup` modal + render-copy substrate become the foundation for the Phase 8-10 mode systems. |
| v6.3.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 6: OSI mode** — the sixth phase on the v5.7.0 / v5.8.0/5.9.0 / v6.0.0 / v6.1.0 / v6.2.0 foundation. Where Phase 5 Trace shows one OSI chip per hop (e.g. `L3 · Network`), Phase 6 OSI mode shows the full 7-layer L1-L7 stack per hop with active/passive distinction + per-layer protocol fields (mock MACs for L2, real IPs for L3) + locked stop-slop activity verbs + a visible encap/decap animation that walks the packet down the stack at source, up-and-down at intermediate routers/switches, and up the stack at destination. Failure pins to the specific OSI layer that owns the fault (no-route → L3, no-cable-path → L1, mac-not-found → L2). The pedagogical target is the N10-009 OSI questions that test "what does a router rewrite vs preserve" (L2 MAC swap visible between adjacent hops while L3 IPs stay constant) and "where does each failure mode originate". **Architecture** (additive to the existing `features/topology-builder-v3.js` IIFE, ~+650 LOC JS + ~+158 LOC CSS vs Phase 5; no new feature modules; `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r10 → r11` at Stage 0): (1) **View-toggle on Trace, not a separate mode machine** — `state.mode` adds `'osi'` as a 5th value (`design | simulate | trace | osi | 3d`); the OSI modebar pill (locked since Phase 1) unlocks. `_openOSI(payload?)` wraps `_openTrace(payload || null)`, sets `state.mode = 'osi'`, adds the `osi-open` body class, re-renders. Trace ↔ OSI toggle is a mode flip — `_traceState` is shared (zero re-init); only the body class + render dispatch differ. `_openTrace` itself does NOT call `_closeOSI` (invariant locked by Stage 11 UAT forEach: every inspector-opener path calls BOTH `_closeTrace` AND `_closeOSI`, but `_openTrace` does not — they share state). (2) **Zero new module-scope state** — `_traceState` gains ONE new field: `osiAnimHandle: null` (12th field; mirrors Phase 5's `rafHandle` but for intra-hop encap/decap rAF). All Phase 5 cancel sites (`_resetTraceState` / `_stepTrace` top-of-fn / `_pauseTrace` / `_endTrace`) extended to clear it alongside `rafHandle` — the emil §8.6 dual-timer discipline now triple-coverage. Plus a parallel `reasonCode` field (13th) added in Stage 7 — captures Phase 3's raw REACH_REASON string from `_startTrace` so `_renderOSIPanel`'s failure-row marking can map to an OSI layer via the §8 lookup. (3) **Render dispatch** in `_renderTracePanel` adds ONE branch: `(state.mode === 'osi') ? _renderOSIPanel() : _renderTraceAnnotation()`. The annotation pane is the swap point — Phase 5's chip-style summary becomes Phase 6's 7-row layer stack. Header (eyebrow + title), controls section (src/dst/Start/Next/Play/End), and hop list (`_renderHopList`) all stay unchanged — shared. (4) **`_renderOSIPanel` empty state** renders the same 7-row DOM with all rows passive + per-row placeholder copy (`Pick a source + destination, then Start to populate this layer`) — same DOM shape as the active view, only content varies. Active state pulls IPs from `state.devices[*].config.ip`, mock MACs from `_genMockMac(devId)` (deterministic djb2 hash → `02:00:00:XX:XX:XX` locally-administered range; zero new schema), cable type from `state.cables[*].type`, calls `_buildLayerStackForHop` for the 7-row descriptor array, marks the failure layer if `_traceState.failedAt === idx` via `_failedReasonToLayer(_traceState.reasonCode)`. (5) **Layer content model** — 4 pure helpers compose the per-hop output: `_activeLayersForDev(dev)` returns the array of layer numbers a device type engages for ICMP (endpoint = `[1,2,3,7]` with L4 explicit `n/a`; switch/ap/wlc = `[1,2]`; router/l3-switch/firewall/vpn = `[1,2,3]`; cloud/internet = `[1,2,3]`). `_hopRole(idx)` returns `'source' | 'intermediate' | 'dest'`. `_verbForLayer(layerNum, role, devType)` returns the locked stop-slop verb string for each (layer, role, devType) triple — 12 verbatim templates per spec §7.4, with `'Filters per policy. Forwards via routing table'`'s **period** load-bearing (UAT inherits the §7.4 rule from Phase 5; tombstones lock out bare `'Wraps with IP'` / `'Rewrites MAC'` variants). `_protoForLayer(layerNum, role, devType, ctx)` returns the role-varying proto string per row — at source `Ethernet · src={srcMac} · dst={nextHopMac}`, at intermediate router `Ethernet · src={routerMacOut} · dst={nextHopMac}` (the visible L2 MAC swap between adjacent hops while L3 IPs stay constant is THE entire pedagogical lesson rendered live), at switch `Ethernet · forwarding table lookup`, at dest `Ethernet · dst={dstMac} matches`. (6) **Motion engine — 3 functions, all rAF-driven, all reduced-motion-gated** (the Opus stage cluster: 8/9/10): `_animateEncap(srcHopId, activeLayers, onDone)` runs the L7→L1 top-down cascade at the source (80ms per active layer, no overlap, `cubic-bezier(0.5, 0, 0.5, 1)` easing). `_animateIntermediate(hopId, deviceType, onDone)` runs the 3-phase decap-up + 100ms pause + re-encap-down at routers/switches (topLayer = 2 for switch/ap/wlc, 3 for router/l3-switch/firewall/vpn; visible "this device touched L1-L3 and forwarded" beat). `_animateDecap(dstHopId, activeLayers, onDone)` runs the mirror L1→L7 bottom-up cascade at the destination. All three capture their `requestAnimationFrame` handle onto `_traceState.osiAnimHandle` so rapid Next clicks cancel cleanly per emil §8.6 interruptibility — and all three fall through to a reduced-motion fast-path (light all relevant layers at once via `_setOSILayerFiring`, fire `onDone` after 80ms — no cascade animation, single static highlight). Wire site: `_stepTrace`'s existing Phase 5 onDone callback (after `_movePacketTracked` settles) adds an OSI branch that dispatches on role to the appropriate animation — runs IN PARALLEL with Phase 5's settle pulse + canvas badge update (neither replaces the other). `_startTrace` adds an OSI initial encap call after `_spawnPacketSvg + _renderTracePanel()`. (7) **`_setOSILayerFiring(layerNum)` DOM helper** (Stage 6) adds `.tb3-osi-layer-firing` class to the matching row, triggers the 80ms `tb3OSILayerSettle` keyframe (accent drop-shadow pulse), cleans up on `animationend` with a 1400ms setTimeout safety net for the reduced-motion path (where CSS sets `animation:none` + a 1200ms static drop-shadow fade). (8) **REACH_REASON → OSI layer mapping** (Stage 7, spec §8) — `_failedReasonToLayer(reason)` lookup: `no-link`/`no-cable-path` → L1; `mac-not-found`/`no-l2-path` → L2; `no-ip`/`no-gateway`/`gateway-not-found`/`different-subnet`/`not-l3`/`no-route`/`no-router-between` → L3; unknown reason defaults to L3 (the most common N+ diagnostic fault domain). The mapped layer's row in `_renderOSIPanel` gets `.is-failure` (2px red left-bar via `::before` + 6% red-tinted bg via `color-mix(in oklab)` + inline reason text). The packet visibly stalls at that layer; Phase 5's `_failDevice` fires in parallel for the canvas device shake + red glow. (9) **5-panel cross-rail mutex** — Phase 5 had 4 (Inspector / Picker / Diagnostic / Simulate). Phase 6 adds OSI as the 5th. Stage 11's forEach UAT lock asserts every inspector-opener path (`_selectDevice` / `_openPicker` / `_openDiagnostic` / `_openSimulate`) calls BOTH `_closeTrace()` AND `_closeOSI()` — any future `_open*` family addition that forgets the OSI teardown trips UAT. The Esc-key handler closes OSI BEFORE Trace (more-specific-first). (10) **Scoped CSS** (Stage 6, ~+158 LOC scoped to `#page-topology-builder-v3`): 4 asymmetric easing tokens declared (`--tb3-osi-ease-encap` / `--tb3-osi-ease-decap-up` / `--tb3-osi-ease-reencap` / `--tb3-osi-ease-decap`); panel + eyebrow + title + 3-cell layer row grid (num / name + proto + verb); 3 variants (`.is-active` accent left-bar via `::before` + accent num/name; `.is-passive` dim text + italic verb; `.is-failure` red bar + red text + red-tint bg + inline reason); `tb3OSILayerSettle` 80ms keyframe; full `@media prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` gate (kills cascade animation, single 1200ms static drop-shadow). Mock MACs (`_genMockMac`) — deterministic djb2 hash of device ID → 3-byte hex → `02:00:00:XX:XX:XX` (locally-administered MAC range, U/L bit set, NOT a real OUI). Zero new storage, zero schema extension on `state.devices`. **Plan-vs-codebase shakeout caught + repaired in-flight by the Stage 13 Playwright suite (Phase 5 precedent held — UAT regex passes don't guarantee runtime correctness)**: (a) `_openOSI` was calling `document.body.classList.add('osi-open')` — wrong element; all rail panel state classes live on `#tb3-body`, not `document.body`. Fixed in both `_openOSI` and `_closeOSI` to target `#tb3-body`. (b) `_openOSI` unconditionally called `_openTrace(payload)` on every invocation, which calls `_initTraceState(null)` and resets `currentHopIdx` to 0 — so the Trace ↔ OSI mid-trace toggle (test 52) was destroying the trace state every flip. Fixed with an `alreadyInTrace` guard: only calls `_openTrace` when entering fresh; otherwise just sets the mode + body class. Two UAT guards from Stage 2 had to be migrated (regex windows widened from `{0,400}` → `{0,600}` to accommodate the new branched implementation) — same regression strength, correct shape. UAT cumulative new asserts = **+89** (baseline 6664 → final 6753). **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+~650 LOC across all Phase 6 commits: `osiAnimHandle` + `reasonCode` state fields + cancel-discipline coverage + OSI modebar unlock + `_openOSI`/`_closeOSI` lifecycle + 5-panel mutex extension + Esc handler + `_genMockMac` + `_hopRole` + `_activeLayersForDev` + `_verbForLayer` + `_protoForLayer` + `_buildLayerStackForHop` + `_renderOSIPanel` + render dispatch + `_setOSILayerFiring` + `_failedReasonToLayer` + `_FAILED_REASON_TO_LAYER` map + `_animateEncap` + `_animateIntermediate` + `_animateDecap` + module exposures for Playwright test reach + 2 dogfood-precedent bug fixes); `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+~158 LOC scoped Phase 6 OSI block: panel layout + 7-row grid + 3 variants + tb3OSILayerSettle keyframe + reduced-motion gate + 4 easing tokens); `tests/uat.js` (+~340 LOC of `_tbv3Phase6Fixtures` IIFE with 5 vm-sandbox fixtures + ~52 P6-prefixed `test()` assertions + forEach mutex lock); `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (+~245 LOC of 8 Playwright tests 46-53 — panel render + active layers + mock MAC + failure pin + reduced-motion + Trace↔OSI toggle + cross-rail); `.superpowers/brainstorm/73986-1779533164/content/phase6-dogfood.html` (NEW 10-step founder smoke); `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase6-osi-design.md` (NEW 446-line design spec); `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase6.md` (NEW 2815-line 16-stage plan, mirroring Phase 5's bite-by-bite discipline). **Tests**: UAT **6753/6753** (was 6664 at v6.2.0 + 89 net new Phase 6 structural guards; spec §12.1 floor was ~35 — comfortably exceeded). Tech-debt clean (no new breaches; 2 pre-existing saas-gated breaches unchanged — `app.js` LOC #138, `styles.css` LOC #55). **Process**: brainstorming (8 shape-of-solution decisions locked via dialogue — view-toggle vs separate mode · all-7-rows vs only-active vs toggleable · replace-annotation vs stack-below vs replace-hops · animated encap/decap vs static vs hybrid · protocol-only vs verb vs verb+fields · auto-enter-Trace vs disabled-until-trace vs hybrid · decap-up+pause+re-encap vs glide-only vs highlight-only · layer-specific failure pin vs all-active-red vs inherit-only) → spec doc (`docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase6-osi-design.md`, 446 lines, 15 sections including locked verbs + REACH_REASON map + motion timing budget) → 16-stage implementation plan (`docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase6.md`, 2815 lines, ALL stages detailed bite-by-bite per founder discipline) → subagent-driven dev (Stages 0-15 walked in one session, 18 commits — **Sonnet for 13 stages, Opus for the motion-engine cluster Stages 8/9/10** per the locked Haiku-banned discipline; subagent stall risk lower this run vs Phase 5 — most subagents completed cleanly first try, the few stalls handled by orchestrator continuation) → Stage 13 Playwright suite caught 2 real runtime contract bugs that UAT regex couldn't see (Phase 5 precedent held: `_openOSI`'s `document.body` vs `#tb3-body` class scoping + Trace↔OSI state-reset gap) — fixed in-flight with the existing Stage 2 UAT guards migrated to lock the correct contract → v6.3.0. **Phase 6 known limitations** (per spec §13 + carried-forward Phase 5 limits): (a) L4-L7 stays passive for ICMP — pedagogically honest (`n/a — ICMP runs directly on IP`) but visually the upper layers feel underutilized. TCP/HTTP support is Phase 6.x. (b) One mock MAC per device — real routers have per-interface MACs. Pedagogical simplification; the L2-vs-L3 demarcation lesson lands without per-interface accuracy. Multi-interface MACs are Phase 6.x or Phase 7. (c) No reply-path animation — destination shows decap + `ICMP echo reply queued` cue at L7 but doesn't animate the reply walking back. Reply-round-trip is Phase 6.x. (d) `_failedReasonToLayer` defaults unknown reasons to L3 silently — future Phase 3 reason codes that need different mapping should add explicit entries. (e) OSI panel scrolls on dense hops (4 active rows × ~62px + 3 passive × ~32px = ~344px on a 320px panel) — protagonist hop is always visible. (f) The spec §9.6 nuance "cascade STOPS at the failing layer" was simplified in implementation to "cascade fires through, layer marks failure on arrival" (one extra layer-pulse beat past the fault). Flagged as Phase 6.x refinement; the failing layer still pin-marks red with the inline reason. **Phase 7+ deferred** (per founder direction): Phase 7 = 3D mode (perspective-shifted trace visualization; Phase 6's per-layer rendering substrate becomes the reusable cascade inside 3D source/dest devices) · Phase 8 = Coach mode (Tier C AI tutor with reachability + Trace + OSI awareness; reads `_failedReasonToLayer` for layer-anchored explanations) · Phase 9 = Grade mode (PBQ-style scoring against Trace + OSI completion criteria; answer keys use `_activeLayersForDev` per role) · Phase 10 = retire v1+v2 from sidebar + delete `features/topology-builder-v2` + delete v1 code from `app.js` (the strangler-fig payoff). **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (feature-module additive JS/CSS — no DB/auth/money/SW-fetch-logic; `sw.js` = universal CACHE_NAME bump from `bump-version.js`) → canonical trunk push, CI-gated. The Topology Builder v3 now ships its sixth phase: Phase 5's per-hop OSI chip (1 row) expands into Phase 6's full L1-L7 stack (7 rows) with animated encap/decap + locked stop-slop layer verbs + layer-specific failure pins — students see the packet visibly build at the source, watch the router rewrite L2 MACs while preserving L3 IPs, and identify exactly which OSI layer owns each failure mode. The Phase 6 substrate (`_buildLayerStackForHop` + `_activeLayersForDev` + `_failedReasonToLayer` + `_setOSILayerFiring` + the 12 locked verbs) becomes the foundation for the Phase 7-10 mode systems and the strangler-fig retirement payoff. |
| v6.2.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 5: Trace mode** — the fifth phase on the v5.7.0 (Phase 1 canvas) + v5.8.0/5.9.0 (Phase 2/2.x scenarios) + v6.0.0 (Phase 3 reachability validator + diagnostic drawer) + v6.1.0 (Phase 4 Simulate engine) foundation. Where Phase 4 Simulate animates the whole packet round-trip end-to-end (one motion per drill, log-row receipts), Phase 5 Trace breaks the same `computePath`-resolved path into one chip per hop, glides the packet 250ms per hop in step mode (600ms in autoplay), and surfaces per-hop teaching content — OSI chip (`L2 · Data Link` / `L3 · Network` / `L7 · Application`), action verb, reason copy with `{dstIp}/{gateway}/{nextIp}` substitution — in a focal annotation pane below the hop list. Failed traces auto-pause, shake the failing device (Phase 4's `_failDevice` reused), red-tint the reason text. Failed Simulate log rows now sprout a "→ Trace" chevron that hands off the failed pair to Trace mode for hop-by-hop investigation (cross-rail mutex auto-closes Simulate). **Architecture** (additive to the existing `features/topology-builder-v3.js` IIFE, ~+700 LOC JS + ~+280 LOC CSS vs Phase 4; no new feature modules; `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r9 → r10` at Stage 0): (1) **Mutually-exclusive rail panel** — `#tb3-trace-panel` joins Inspector / Picker / Diagnostic / Simulate as a 320px right-anchored slide-in panel (`body.trace-open` class, `position:absolute + transform:translateX(100%)→0` overlay matching Simulate's pattern from Phase 4; reduced-motion neutralizes the transition). Five rail panels now; the cross-rail mutex is symmetric — `_openPicker` / `_openDiagnostic` / `_openSimulate` / `_selectDevice` (the inspector-opener) all call `_closeTrace()` when `body.trace-open` is set, and `_openTrace` removes the four other classes in one sweep. (2) **Module-scope ephemeral state `_traceState`** — 9 keys (`srcId` / `dstId` / `protocol: 'ping'` / `hops: []` / `currentHopIdx: 0` / `failedAt: null` / `reasons: {}` / `mode: 'idle'|'step'|'play'|'paused'|'done'` / `packet: null` / `rafHandle: null` / `autoplayTimer: null`); **zero localStorage writes** — Trace is a transient drill, no durable user data. Initialized by `_initTraceState(payload)` (Stage 1) which accepts an optional `{srcId, dstId, protocol}` payload from the Sim→Trace handoff; reset by `_resetTraceState()` (clears rAF + autoplay timer + packet, restores schema defaults). (3) **Lifecycle handlers** — `_openTrace(payload?)` (cross-rail close + mode='trace' + `_initTraceState` + `_renderTracePanel` + modebar repaint); `_closeTrace()` (class remove + `_resetTraceState` + mode='design' + modebar repaint); Esc handler closes Trace when `body.trace-open`. (4) **Render pipeline** in `_renderTracePanel` builds: header (`TRACE` eyebrow + Fraunces "Trace mode" + × close), controls section (`_renderTraceControls`: src/dst `<select>`s + ping protocol pill + 4 buttons Start/Next/Play/End), hop list (`_renderHopList`: `<ol class="tb3-trace-hops">` with one `<li class="tb3-trace-hop">` per hop, mono number + hostname label + `.is-current` / `.is-failed` / `.is-done` state classes, inline `--tb3-hop-idx` CSS var driving a 200ms staggered entrance keyframe at 40ms cascade), annotation pane (`_renderTraceAnnotation`: eyebrow `Hop N of M` + ink title + bronze-outlined mono OSI chip + action + reason with `.is-failure` red variant). All buttons wired via idempotent `.onclick =` assignment in `_wireTracePanel` (Phase 4 pattern locked by CLAUDE.md regression-guard tombstones); Play button text + handler toggle between `_playTrace` and `_pauseTrace` based on `_traceState.mode === 'play'`. (5) **Motion handlers**: `_startTrace` calls Phase 3's `computePath(srcId, dstId, state)`, normalizes Phase 3's actual return shape (see §dogfood-caught regression below), spawns an amber packet via Phase 4's `_spawnPacketSvg('amber')` / `_devCenter(srcId)`, sets mode='step', re-renders panel. `_stepTrace` advances `currentHopIdx`, glides the packet via `_movePacketTracked(el, fromPt, toPt, durMs, onDone)` (a sibling re-implementation of Phase 4's `_movePacket` — re-implemented because the original doesn't expose its `requestAnimationFrame` handle; this version stores the handle on `_traceState.rafHandle` so rapid Next clicks can `cancelAnimationFrame` the in-flight glide cleanly per the emil §8.6 interruptibility discipline; cubic-bezier ease-in-out approximated as `t < 0.5 ? 2*t*t : 1 - Math.pow(-2*t+2, 2)/2`), with duration `isAutoplay ? 600 : 250` ms per spec §8.1/§8.2; on settle, fires `_renderSettlePulse(hopId)` (re-add `.tb3-trace-settle` class to retrigger the 80ms accent drop-shadow keyframe, with reduced-motion fallback to a 1.5s static glow), updates the per-hop canvas badge via `_updateHopBadge` (14px SVG circle with mono number, accent bronze normally, red on failed hop, `pointer-events:none` so it doesn't steal canvas clicks), and triggers `_failHop` if `toHopIdx === _traceState.failedAt`. `_playTrace` kicks a `setTimeout(tick, 200)` pre-roll then chains `setTimeout(tick, 600 + 120)` (literal addition, NOT 720 — locked by UAT regex) for the autoplay loop, with tick() re-checking `_traceState.mode === 'play'` at the top so external `_pauseTrace` / `_failHop` can bail cleanly mid-cycle. `_pauseTrace` clears both `autoplayTimer` AND `rafHandle` (the emil §8.6 dual-timer discipline — every motion-cancelling action must clear both). `_endTrace` same teardown + despawns the packet. `_failHop(hopIdx, reasonText)` reuses Phase 4's `_failDevice(hopId, reasonText)` (200ms shake keyframe + 1.2s red drop-shadow glow, with reduced-motion gate), auto-pauses if currently in autoplay, captures the reason on `_traceState.reasons[hopIdx]` as a safety net, re-renders panel so the annotation switches to the red-tinted reason. (6) **Locked stop-slop copy** per spec §7.4: `_actionForDevice` returns `'Originates ICMP echo request'` (source) / `'Receives ICMP echo, sends reply'` (destination) / `'Forwards via MAC table'` (switch) / `'Forwards via routing table'` (router/l3-switch) / `'Filters and forwards'` (firewall/vpn — NOT "Inspects + forwards"; UAT tombstones the old phrasing); `_reasonForDevice` returns `'Targets {dstIp} via default gateway {gw}'` (source) / `'Replies to {srcIp}'` (destination) / `'Permits per policy. Egress {nextIp}'` (firewall/vpn — the **period** after "policy" is load-bearing, the §7.4 rule "period breaks the chain", UAT asserts `Permits per policy\. Egress`) / `'Egress port toward {nextIp}'` (switch) / `'Egress to {nextIp}'` (generic). Failure reasons override via `_traceState.reasons[idx]` populated from Phase 3's REACH_REASON_TEMPLATES at start time. (7) **Sim→Trace handoff** (Stage 11) — `_motionPing`'s two failure branches (reduced-motion + animated) now include a `pair: {path, protocol, failedAt, failReason}` field on the `_appendLogEntry` payload; `_renderSimLog` emits a `.tb3-sim-log-trace-this` chevron at the end of every row where `entry.failure && entry.pair`; the delegated `logHost.onclick` handler has a Trace branch (placed before the existing re-play branch so the chevron click doesn't double-fire) that unpacks `srcId` from `entry.pair.path[0]` and `dstId` from `entry.pair.path[length - 1]` and calls `_openTrace(payload)` — the cross-rail mutex auto-closes Simulate. ARP and DHCP motion functions deliberately untouched; Phase 5 ships ping-only handoff, others queued for Phase 5.x. **Subagent-execution Phase 3-surface schema fixes** (caught + adapted by the Stage 14 Playwright suite — would have shipped silently otherwise; UAT regex alone couldn't have caught these because they're runtime contract gaps): (a) `_getState` was referenced from `_renderTracePanel` / `_renderHopList` / `_renderTraceAnnotation` / `_startTrace` (every Phase 5 render helper) but ONLY existed as an inline function on the registration object exposure — internal callers `ReferenceError`-ed at runtime as soon as `_openTrace` fired. Fix: added a sibling `function _getState() { return state; }` inside the IIFE near the `state` declaration, so all render helpers can call it. (b) `_startTrace`'s `_traceState.failedAt = (result && typeof result.failedAt === 'number') ? result.failedAt : null` check was structurally wrong — Phase 3's `computePath` returns `failedAt` as a **device-ID string** (not a numeric index), so the `typeof === 'number'` test was always false, meaning `_traceState.failedAt` was ALWAYS null in practice. Trace silently swallowed every Phase 3 failure code; the entire failure beat was unreachable. Fix: `_startTrace` now normalizes — populates `_traceState.hops = [srcId]` when Phase 3 returns no hops field on failure (so `_renderHopList` has something to mark), and converts the device-ID `failedAt` to an INDEX in that hops array via `hops.indexOf(failedAt)`. The downstream consumers (`_canStepFurther` / `_renderHopList.is-failed` / `_traceState.reasons[idx]`) all expect a numeric index, so the conversion happens at the boundary. (c) Stage 4 UAT regex migrated from the precise `_traceState\.hops\s*=\s*\(result && Array\.isArray\(result\.hops\)\)` lock to a more permissive `Array\.isArray\(result\.hops\)` lock — same regression strength (still asserts the `result.hops` field is being read), looser on the exact LHS shape because the failure-handling rewrite needed an `if/else` branch the old single-line regex couldn't accommodate. **Stage 12 cross-rail mutex audit caught one more real bug**: `_openSimulate` was removing the `trace-open` class manually via `body.classList.remove('trace-open')` but never calling `_closeTrace()`, so when the user switched from Trace to Simulate mid-trace the Trace state was not torn down — `_traceState.rafHandle` + `autoplayTimer` + packet element + the `_traceState` object itself leaked between modes. The Stage 2 UAT guard at line 21815 had only locked the weaker `classList.remove` check, missing the teardown gap. Fix: `_openSimulate` now calls `_closeTrace()` conditionally (`if (body.classList.contains('trace-open'))`) matching the proven `_openPicker` pattern; the Stage 2 UAT guard was MIGRATED to assert `_closeTrace()` call (same regression strength, stronger contract); a new forEach lock asserts all 4 inspector-opener paths (`_selectDevice` / `_openPicker` / `_openDiagnostic` / `_openSimulate`) call `_closeTrace()` so any future `_open*` family addition that forgets the teardown trips UAT. (`_openInspector` never existed as a separate function in this codebase — `_selectDevice` is the inspector-opener path; the plan's expectation was adapted.) **Stage 14 test-topology adaptation**: Playwright test 40 (Play/Pause with a 3-device path) initially used a router as the middle device — Phase 3's BFS-through-L2-cables algorithm stops at L3 boundaries, so a router mid-path on the same /24 subnet blocked the L2 walk from workstation to server. Test now uses a switch (L2-transparent) for the middle device so the BFS walks d1→d2→d3 cleanly. The plan's example fixture had the same router; flagged as a plan oversight (the dogfood scenario uses a real router on a different subnet which IS the legitimate use case for routing). **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+~700 LOC across all Phase 5 commits: state schema + lifecycle + mutex + panel scaffold + scoped CSS rev bump + controls render + wiring + `_startTrace` + `_renderHopList` + `_stepTrace` + `_movePacketTracked` + `_renderSettlePulse` + `_updateHopBadge` + `_clearHopBadges` + `_renderTraceAnnotation` + `_osiChipForDevice` + `_actionForDevice` + `_reasonForDevice` + `_canStepFurther` + `_buildDeviceOptions` + `_playTrace` + `_pauseTrace` + `_endTrace` + `_failHop` + Sim→Trace chevron in `_renderSimLog` + `_motionPing.pair` payload + log click handler Trace branch + `_getState` internal helper + `_openSimulate → _closeTrace` cross-rail fix + module exposures for `_openTrace`/`_closeTrace`/`_startTrace`/`_stepTrace`/`_playTrace`/`_pauseTrace`/`_endTrace`); `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+~280 LOC scoped: panel slide-in + controls block + dropdowns + protocol pill + 4 buttons with `:active` press + hover gate + focus-visible + disabled state + hop list + state classes + 40ms stagger keyframe + reduced-motion gate + `tb3TraceSettle` 80ms accent-glow keyframe + reduced-motion fallback + annotation pane + OSI chip + `.is-failure` variant + 14px badge + Sim→Trace chevron); `.superpowers/brainstorm/73986-1779533164/content/phase5-dogfood.html` (NEW 10-step founder smoke); `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase5-trace-design.md` (NEW design spec); `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-23-tb-v3-phase5.md` (NEW 16-stage plan, 3127 lines). **Tests**: UAT **6664/6664** (was 6570 at v6.1.0 + ~94 Phase 5 structural guards). Playwright **chromium 153/153** (was 143 at v6.1.0 + 10 new Phase 5 tests). The Topology Builder v3 now ships its fifth phase: Phase 4's whole-packet Simulate animation gets a per-hop counterpart in Trace, and a failed Simulate ping is one click away from a hop-by-hop investigation via the chevron handoff — the loop tightens from "see what's broken" (Phase 3 diagnostic drawer) to "see the packet die" (Phase 4 Simulate animation) to "see exactly which hop owns the failure and why" (Phase 5 Trace). The Trace per-hop framing + locked OSI/action/reason copy become the substrate for the Phase 6-9 systems (OSI overlays the L1-L7 stack at each hop; Coach contextualizes the failure copy with Tier C tutoring; Grade scores PBQ attempts against the trace path students produce). |
| v6.1.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 4: Simulate mode** — the fourth phase on the v5.7.0 (Phase 1 canvas) + v5.8.0/5.9.0 (Phase 2/2.x scenarios catalog) + v6.0.0 (Phase 3 reachability validator + diagnostic drawer) foundation. Phase 3 turned the canvas into a learning instrument (the completion pill flips GOALS MET / N TO GO live as the founder edits); Phase 4 animates the same paths the validator computes — three per-protocol motion signatures (ping round-trip + ARP burst/fan-out/reply + DHCP DORA), a live Wireshark-style log, and a Validator Preview that plays every required cable type-pair sequentially with click-to-replay on individual rows. The reachability engine + diagnostic drawer (Phase 3) become the substrate; Simulate adds the moving-packet layer on top. **Architecture** (additive to the existing `features/topology-builder-v3.js` IIFE, ~+800 LOC vs Phase 3; no new feature modules; `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r8 → r9` at Stage 0): (1) **Mutually-exclusive rail panel** — `#tb3-simulate-panel` joins Inspector / Picker / Diagnostic-drawer as a 320px right-anchored slide-in panel (`body.simulate-open` class, `position:absolute + transform:translateX(100%)→0` overlay rather than the grid-column reflow of the other panels — read-heavy panel, no canvas reflow needed; documented inline in CSS). The Stage 2 mutual-exclusion guards (`_openPicker`/`_openDiagnostic`/`_selectDevice` auto-call `_closeSimulate`) keep the single-track UX. (2) **Module-scope ephemeral state `_simState`** — 8 keys (`currentPacket` rAF handle / `previewQueue` / `playing` / `log` cap 200 / `drillSrcId` / `drillDstId` / `drillProtocol: 'ping'` / `lastReport`); **zero localStorage writes** (UAT tombstone guards both the `STORAGE.*` namespace and the `nplus_tb_v3_sim*` key space — Simulate is a transient drill, not durable user data). (3) **Animation engine** (`_spawnPacketSvg(color)` → returns an SVG `<circle>` with class `.tb3-packet` + drop-shadow; `_movePacket(el, fromPt, toPt, durMs, onDone)` drives the move via `requestAnimationFrame` with cubic-bezier ease and updates `_simState.currentPacket` each frame; `_despawnPacket(el)` removes; `_devCenter(devId)` returns canvas-space center). The `_reducedMotion()` helper checks `matchMedia('(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)')` and every motion fn has a log-only fallback. (4) **`_animatePacket(spec)` orchestrator** dispatches via lookup `{ping:_motionPing, arp:_motionArp, dhcp:_motionDhcp}` (NOT a switch — future-extensible to OSI/Trace overlays). The spec carries `path`, `protocol`, `failedAt`, `failReason`, `onLog`, `onComplete`. (5) **Per-protocol motion signatures**: `_motionPing` plays a round-trip (src → hops → dst with a 600ms hop duration + 80ms settle pulse at dst → hops → src, then despawn — single amber dot `oklch(0.74 0.13 65)`); `_motionArp` plays 4 phases (200ms broadcast ring at src expanding 6→96px while fading + 300ms fan-out green dots to every `_sameSubnetDevices(srcId)` member + 100ms opacity-flash on each receiver + 300ms unicast amber reply from dst back to src — `oklch(0.7 0.15 145)` green); `_motionDhcp` plays four-stage DORA (Discover broadcast ring at client → 120ms gap → Offer unicast server-to-client → 120ms gap → Request broadcast ring at client → 120ms gap → Ack unicast server-to-client — `oklch(0.62 0.16 250)` blue; failure injected at Ack stage logs "DHCP failed" with reason). Each motion has an inline reduced-motion path that fires log-only via a `setTimeout` cascade. (6) **Real `_appendLogEntry` + `_renderSimLog`** — entries are `{ts, protocol, text, failure?, pair?}` shape; `_appendLogEntry` caps at 200 (`.shift()` when over) then calls `_renderSimLog` which rebuilds the row list with millisecond timestamps + `data-log-idx` attributes + a `·`/`✗` prefix + auto-scroll to bottom + XSS-safe `_escAttr` on text. Log host stays a single DOM element across renders so the `.onclick` delegated handler persists. (7) **Drill controls** (`_renderDrillControls`): src/dst `<select>` dropdowns auto-populated from `state.devices` (with the prior `_simState.drillSrcId/dstId` preserved across re-renders via the `selected` attribute), a 3-button protocol toggle (`.tb3-sim-proto.on` for the active one), and a Send button (`_updateSendEnabled` toggles `disabled` when src/dst not both set or are equal). `_onDrillSend` calls Phase 3's `computePath(srcId, dstId, state)` (which returns `{ok, hops, reason?, failedAt?}` — the field is `hops` not `path` as the plan first assumed; adapted) and hands the spec to `_animatePacket`. (8) **Canvas-click shortcut** — when `state.mode === 'simulate'`, clicking any `.tb3-dev[data-device-id]` on canvas fills the next-empty drill slot (src → dst → replaces dst). (9) **Failure UX** — `_failDevice(devId, reasonText)` adds a 200ms `tb3SimFail` shake keyframe (`translateX(±3px)` × 4 cycle) + a 1.2s red glow `drop-shadow(0 0 10px var(--tb3-pkt-failure))` that fades via `transition` (reduced-motion path: glow only, 1.5s static); `_reachReasonText(failedAt, reason, srcId, dstId)` wraps Phase 3's `REACH_REASON_TEMPLATES` (function-valued map — adapted at call time for either function or string template shape) with `srcLabel/dstLabel/failedLabel/srcCidr/dstCidr` context to produce human-readable failure copy in the log row. Wired into all 3 motion fns at their existing failure branches. (10) **Validator Preview** — `#tb3-sim-preview-section` (`hidden` unless `state.intent === 'lab' && state.activeScenarioId`); button toggles between "Replay validator paths" and "Stop"; `_runValidatorPreview()` reads the active scenario's `completion.requiredCables`, calls `computeReachability(state, completion)` (which returns `{complete, failures}` — the field is `failures` and the success-flag is `complete` not `ok` as the plan first assumed; adapted), builds a queue of pairs (smart-pick: first device of each type), then `_runNextPreviewPair()` plays one pair at a time with a 600ms gap between (200ms in reduced-motion). Each completed pair appends a re-play-shaped log entry (`pair: {path, protocol, failedAt, failReason}` payload); log-row click looks up the entry and fires `_animatePacket` to re-play that specific pair. Stop clears the queue, cancels the in-flight rAF, and restores the button. (11) **Idempotent wiring** — `_wireSimulate` uses `.onclick =` / `.onchange =` direct assignment for every control (close button, src/dst dropdowns, protocol buttons, Send button, preview button, log host) — NOT `addEventListener` — so multiple `_openSimulate` calls don't accumulate listeners on the same DOM nodes. This pattern was caught + locked in the Stage-1/2 quality polish before Stage 3 added handler-heavy wiring; the dogfood fix at Stage 13 reinforced it (canvas-click branch now calls `_renderSimulatePanel()` not `_renderDrillControls()` so re-wiring runs after the DOM rebuild). (12) **Test-only exposures** added to the feature registration object: `_renderCanvas` (Stage 3, for tests 28-30 to push devices then re-render), `_closeSimulate` (Stage 11, because the Esc-key path guards on the page-active class which Playwright can't satisfy from `page.keyboard.press('Escape')`), and `_openPicker` (Stage 11, because `#tb3-rrail-scenarios` is `display:none` while `simulate-open` so the picker can't be opened via a real UI click while Simulate is active). Same pattern as Phase 2's `_getState`/`_setState`/`_deleteSelected` exposures. **Plan-vs-Phase-3-surface schema adaptations** (caught + adapted cleanly across 3 stages, no Phase 3 surfaces touched): (a) `computePath` returns `result.hops` not `result.path` (Stage 4 adapted in `_onDrillSend`); (b) `computeReachability` returns `{complete, failures}` not `{ok, ...}` (Stage 9); (c) `requiredCables` schema uses `from`/`to` not `fromType`/`toType` (Stage 9 adapted in `_runValidatorPreview` queue-builder). All 3 documented in the resume doc; future motion-engine stages will inherit the correct names. **Dogfood-caught regression fixed before ship**: founder walked the 10-step dogfood and reported "each step works successfully — the only thing is that you have to refresh the page every time to successfully pass each step." Root cause: canvas-click branch (Task 3.3) called `_renderDrillControls()` which rebuilt `host.innerHTML` and destroyed the `<select>`/`<button>` DOM elements that had `.onchange`/`.onclick` handlers attached; `_wireSimulate` was NOT called after the rebuild so the new controls were silently inert. Same gap existed in `_renderCanvas` — dropping a new device from the palette while Simulate was open updated `state.devices` but the panel's dropdowns weren't refreshed to include the new device. **Fix** (commit `9b81445`, 2 lines): canvas-click branch now calls `_renderSimulatePanel()` (which calls `_renderDrillControls` + `_renderSimLog` + `_wireSimulate` — full refresh + re-wire); `_renderCanvas` end gains `if (state.mode === 'simulate') _renderSimulatePanel();` so any state mutation that re-renders the canvas also keeps the Simulate panel in sync. The `.onclick =` idempotency pattern from the Stage-1/2 polish meant the re-wire couldn't double-bind anything — clean fix. **Lesson (locked)**: any handler that calls a panel-section-rebuild render (innerHTML replace on an element containing wired controls) MUST also call the panel-level wire function — partial render + skipped wire creates silently inert controls. **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+~800 LOC across all Phase 4 commits: rail panel scaffold + open/close + mode-bar wire + Esc + mutual exclusion + drill controls + canvas click shortcut + animation primitives + log + 3 motion fns + failure UX + Validator Preview + Stage-13 dogfood fix + 4 test exposures); `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+~200 LOC scoped to `#page-topology-builder-v3 #tb3-simulate-panel`: palette tokens + panel layout + slide-in + drill controls + log + shake keyframe + reduced-motion gates); `tests/uat.js` (+13 Phase 4 structural guards in `_tbv3Phase4Fixtures` IIFE with `tbv3SrcP4` / `tbv3Css` module-scope consts — covers panel render fns + canvas-click dispatch + cross-rail exit count + motion fn definitions + failure UX + reduced-motion JS + reduced-motion CSS + schema + no-localStorage tombstone); `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (+10 Playwright DOM tests 26-35 — panel open/close + Drill controls + Send-gating + click-shortcut + packet element + Validator Preview Lab-only + sequenced playback + Esc exit + Picker exit); `.superpowers/brainstorm/93179-1779476357/content/phase4-dogfood.html` (NEW 10-step founder smoke). **Tests**: UAT **6570/6570** (was 6557 at v6.0.0 + 13 Phase 4 guards). Playwright **chromium 143/143** (was 133 at v6.0.0 + 10 new Phase 4 tests). Tech-debt clean (no new breaches; 2 pre-existing saas-gated breaches unchanged — `app.js` LOC #138, `styles.css` LOC #55). **Process**: brainstorming (7 shape decisions locked via visual companion — hybrid lens · ping+ARP+DHCP · right-rail panel · dropdown+click shortcut · per-protocol signatures · live log · sequenced playback) → spec doc → 13-stage implementation plan (ALL stages detailed bite-by-bite per founder discipline) → subagent-driven dev (Stages 0-12 walked across two sessions, 31 commits — **Sonnet for mechanical stages, Opus for the motion-engine stages 5/6/7** per the locked Haiku-banned discipline; one polish commit caught + fixed the listener-accumulation pattern before Stage 3 added handler-heavy wiring) → live founder dogfood (10 steps, all pass) → 1 dogfood-caught regression (panel handler re-wire) fixed in 1 commit → v6.1.0. **Phase 4 known limitations** (deferred to later phases): (a) `_motionPing` only handles failure when `spec.failedAt === path[path.length - 1]` (the destination). If a router mid-path is the failure point (Phase 3's `computePath` does return mid-hop failedAt), the animation runs the full round-trip without acknowledging the mid-hop break — the log row still shows the failure via `REACH_REASON_TEMPLATES`, just the animation doesn't shake the failing device. Phase 5 (Trace mode, per-hop visualization) will surface mid-hop failures more clearly. (b) `_renderSimLog` rebuilds the full DOM on every entry — fine for human-paced drills (200-entry cap) but will thrash on the Stage 9 Validator batch-fire path if a scenario has many pairs; Phase 5+ may want to switch to incremental appendChild. (c) Test 33 (Esc exits Simulate) drives via the exposed `_closeSimulate` function rather than the real `page.keyboard.press('Escape')` because `_wireGlobalKeys` guards on the page-active class which Playwright can't reliably satisfy — the real-keypress behavior is still covered manually in dogfood step 10. **Phase 5+ deferred** (per founder direction: each phase is independently shippable and gets its own dogfood pass, re-planned bite-by-bite after the prior phase ships): Phase 5 = Trace mode (per-hop visualization with packet-flow choreography over the same `computePath` substrate) · Phase 6 = OSI mode (per-layer overlay annotating each hop with the OSI layer in play) · Phase 7 = 3D mode · Phase 8 = Coach mode (Tier C AI tutor with reachability + failure-reason awareness) · Phase 9 = Grade mode (PBQ-style scoring against scenario completion criteria) · Phase 10 = retire v1+v2 from sidebar + delete `features/topology-builder-v2` + delete v1 code from `app.js` (the strangler-fig payoff). **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (feature-module additive JS/CSS — no DB/auth/money/SW-fetch-logic; `sw.js` = universal CACHE_NAME bump from `bump-version.js`) → canonical trunk push, CI-gated. The Topology Builder v3 now ships its fourth phase: Phase 3's reachability validator (the diagnostic drawer showing what's broken) and Phase 4's Simulate engine (animating the paths the validator computes — success motions for ping/ARP/DHCP, failure UX for the broken ones) close the loop — students load a scenario, watch the panel/animation tell them what's working and what isn't, fix the broken hop, watch the Validator Preview replay all required pairs green. The animation engine + log + Validator Preview become the substrate for the Phase 5-9 mode systems (Trace + OSI overlay the per-hop detail; Coach contextualizes failures using `REACH_REASON_TEMPLATES`; Grade scores PBQ attempts against scenario completion). |
| v6.0.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 3: Lab completion validator + diagnostic drawer** — the third phase on the v5.7.0 (Phase 1 canvas) + v5.8.0 (Phase 2 scenarios picker) + v5.9.0 (Phase 2.x full catalog) foundation. Phase 2's `checkCompletion` was structural-only (required devices present + device-count match + required cable type-pairs wired); Phase 3 turns it into a real L2/L3 **reachability simulator**: for every required cable type-pair the validator computes a path across the topology and verifies the packet can actually route. The completion pill flips between **GOALS MET** (every required pair reaches) and **N TO GO** (count = missing devices + count mismatches + missing cables + reachability failures) live as the founder edits. **Architecture** (additive to the existing `features/topology-builder-v3.js` IIFE, ~+1200 LOC vs Phase 2; no new feature modules; `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r7→r8`): (1) **Reachability engine** — `computePath(srcId, dstId, state)` walks the topology from src device through cables + intermediate L3/L2 hops to dst, returning `{ok, reason?, failedAt?}`. Reads `device.config.gateway` for L3 next-hop; on L3 hop, finds the device whose interface IP matches the gateway (must be L3-capable type — router/l3-switch/firewall/vpn). On L2 hop, walks cables to find directly-connected device on the same subnet. Returns failure with templated reason on first broken hop: `no-gateway` (workstation's `config.gateway` is empty), `gateway-not-found` (gateway IP doesn't match any L3 device's interface), `not-l3` (gateway device exists but is L2-only), `different-subnet` (intermediate hop's interface isn't on the expected subnet), etc. Each reason maps to a human-readable template in `REACH_REASON_TEMPLATES` (e.g. `'%srcLabel has no default gateway.'`). (2) **`computeReachability(state, completion)`** — for each `requiredCable` type-pair in the scenario completion block, picks a representative source + destination device of each type, calls `computePath`, collects all failures. Smart-pick strategy: succeeds if any representative pair can route per cable type-pair (not full-mesh) — handles L3 transit paths (spine-leaf, multi-hop) without requiring exhaustive per-pair config. (3) **`checkCompletion(state, completion)`** wires `computeReachability` into the existing Phase 2 structural validator: returns `{complete, missingDevices, deviceCountMismatch, missingCables, reachabilityFailures}` with `complete=true` only if all four arrays are empty. The completion pill at `_renderCompletionPill` reads `reachabilityFailures.length` into the N TO GO count. (4) **Diagnostic drawer** (`_renderDiagnosticDrawer` + `_wireDiagnosticDrawer`): right-anchored 380px slide-in panel (same mechanism as Inspector + picker, mutually exclusive — only one rail panel open at a time). DOM appended to `_renderWorkspace` as `#tb3-diagnostic`, CSS-shown via `body.diagnostic-open` class. Renders either the empty (all-passing) state (`DIAGNOSTICS / Goals met` + body `All paths reachable` + sub `Every required cable type-pair has a working route` + footer `UPDATED LIVE AS YOU EDIT`) or a list of `.tb3-diagnostic-row` buttons (one per failure, each showing `{srcLabel} → {dstLabel}` + the templated reason). Drawer opens on pill click (only in Lab mode); failure-row click closes drawer + auto-selects the failing device via `_selectDevice(devId)` so Inspector opens for direct fix; × button + Esc close. Drawer auto-refreshes on every `_renderCompletionPill` call (any state mutation that affects reachability re-renders the drawer if open). CSS scroll constraints applied per the v5.9.1 grid-flex shrink lesson (`min-height:0` on the drawer body so its `overflow-y:auto` engages — the catalog rebuild lesson). Reduced-motion gate neutralizes the slide-in transition. (5) **IP back-fill across all 25 scenarios** (8 commits, separable for clean rollback): every device in every scenario now has valid `config.ip` + `config.mask` + `config.gateway` so the validator can actually run. Coverage: topology (star/mesh/ring/p2p), architecture (3-tier/spine-leaf/collapsed-core/soho), WAN (hub-spoke/mpls/partial-mesh/dual-isp/dual-isp-failover), cloud (hybrid/public-only/multi-cloud/direct-connect), security (dmz/zero-trust/bastion/nac), wireless (controller-bss-ess/mesh/p2p-bridge), VLAN (router-on-stick/l3-switch-svi). Subnet conventions per scenario family (e.g. `192.168.X0.0/24` for endpoint LANs, `10.X.X.X/30` for WAN P2P transits, distinct subnets per VLAN/zone for routed scenarios). (6) **`_autoFillIp` drop wire** — Free Build devices dropped via the palette get auto-filled IP + gateway too (router `192.168.10.1/24`, workstation `192.168.10.10/24` with gateway `192.168.10.1`) so completion logic works on Free Build → scenario migrations. **Dogfood-caught regressions (2 fixed this session before ship — the locked verification discipline working as designed)**: (a) **Cable mode click handler in Free Build** — the device drag mousedown handler at `_wireDragToCanvas` called `_renderCanvas()` on every device mousedown, which replaces the SVG via `svg.innerHTML = ... ; svg.innerHTML += ...` and detaches the original `<g class="tb3-dev">` element. When the subsequent `click` event fired on the cable handler, `e.target.closest('.tb3-dev')` walked a broken parent chain and returned null — handler bailed at `if (!g) return;`, `pendingFromId` never got set, no cable ever fired. The `_wirePanZoom()` handler at the same location already used the cursor-mode guard `if (wrap.style.cursor === 'crosshair') return;` to skip in cable mode; the device drag handler just missed it. **Fix**: 1-line guard mirroring the pan handler pattern. **Lesson (locked)**: any mousedown handler that calls `_renderCanvas()` (or any DOM-replacing render) must guard against modes that own subsequent click events on the same target. Future TB v3 mode systems (Simulate/Trace/OSI) that take over click events MUST add equivalent guards. (b) **Inspector × close button** — no explicit close affordance on the right-rail Inspector panel; founder-flagged UX gap during the dogfood walkthrough. **Fix**: × button in the Inspector header, wired to clear `state.selectedId` + re-render (same path as the existing Esc-key deselect at `_wireGlobalKeys`). **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+~1200 LOC across all Phase 3 commits: reachability engine + diagnostic drawer render/wire + 25 scenario IP back-fills + `_autoFillIp` drop wire + cable-mode click guard + Inspector × close button) · `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+drawer styles + scroll constraints) · `tests/uat.js` (+10 Phase 3 structural guards) · `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (+8 Playwright DOM tests covering drawer + Inspector + reduced-motion + scroll constraints) · `.superpowers/brainstorm/17327-1779282193/content/phase3-dogfood.html` (10-step founder smoke) · `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-20-tb-v3-phase3-design.md` (NEW spec) · `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-20-tb-v3-phase3.md` (NEW plan, ALL stages detailed bite-by-bite per founder discipline). **Tests**: UAT **6557/6557** (was 6500 at v5.9.1 + 10 new Phase 3 guards across reachability + drawer + IP back-fill assertions). Playwright **chromium 133/133** (was 117 at v5.9.1 + 16 new Phase 3 tests across two commits — 8 structural guards + 8 DOM tests). tech-debt clean. **Process**: brainstorming (Phase 3 spec section locked from Phase 2 follow-up direction) → spec doc → 10-stage implementation plan (ALL stages detailed bite-by-bite, no "outlined only" tasks — same discipline as Phase 2) → subagent-driven dev (Stages 0-9 walked across multiple sessions, 30 commits) → live founder dogfood (Steps 1-10) → 2 founder-caught regressions fixed mid-dogfood (cable mode + Inspector × button) → 10-step dogfood walked end-to-end with all steps passing → v6.0.0. **Phase 3 known limitation**: smart-pick reachability succeeds if ANY representative pair can route per cable type-pair; it does NOT verify every possible pair routes for scenarios with multiple subnets/VLANs (spine-leaf two-spine-to-spine routing, distant-router reachability across multiple hops). A future Phase 3b can tighten this by adding static-route configuration to the scenario definitions so the validator can verify full-mesh reachability explicitly. **Phase 4+ deferred** (per founder direction: each phase is independently shippable and gets its own dogfood pass, re-planned bite-by-bite after the prior phase ships): Phase 4 = Simulate mode (live packet animation, ping/ARP/DHCP) · Phase 5 = Trace mode (per-hop visualization, packet-flow animation) · Phase 6 = OSI mode (per-layer overlay) · Phase 7 = 3D mode · Phase 8 = Coach mode (Tier C AI tutor with reachability awareness) · Phase 9 = Grade mode (PBQ-style scoring against scenario completion) · Phase 10 = retire v1+v2 from sidebar + delete features/topology-builder-v2 + delete v1 code from app.js (the strangler-fig payoff). **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (feature-module additive JS/CSS — no DB/auth/money; sw.js = universal CACHE_NAME bump from bump-version.js) → canonical trunk push, CI-gated. The Topology Builder v3 now ships its third phase: the canvas foundation (Phase 1) + scenarios catalog (Phase 2/2.x) becomes a real learning instrument — students load a scenario, edit the canvas, get live reachability feedback via the diagnostic drawer, fix what's wrong, watch the pill flip back to GOALS MET. The reachability engine + diagnostic drawer become the substrate for the Phase 4-9 mode systems (Simulate animates the same paths the validator computes; Trace + OSI overlay the per-hop detail; Coach contextualizes failures; Grade scores PBQ attempts). |
| v5.9.1 | **TB v3 picker scroll fix** — founder-caught hotfix from v5.9.0 dogfood: the right-rail Scenarios picker showed Topology Types + Architectures + the WAN header but the bottom of the catalog (rest of WAN, Cloud, Wireless, Security, VLAN — 12 of 25 scenarios) was unreachable. No scrollbar engaged, no touch-scroll, no keyboard scroll. **Root cause (systematic-debugging Phase 1 evidence)**: classic CSS Grid + Flex `overflow:auto` gotcha exposed once the catalog grew from 8 (v5.8.0) to 25 (v5.9.0). `.tb3-picker` is a grid item; CSS Grid items have `min-height: auto` (= content size) by default, so the picker grew to `clientHeight: 2203px` to fit all scenarios. The parent `#page-topology-builder-v3` has `overflow:hidden` from the Phase 1 full-viewport takeover, so anything past viewport height was clipped invisibly. The inner `#tb3-picker-list` had `overflow-y:auto` but no overflow existed within it because the list had grown to full content height (no constraint from its flex parent). At 8 scenarios (~800px content vs ~1100px viewport) the bug was latent — content fit within viewport so clipping was invisible. At 25 scenarios (~2200px content) the bottom 1100px was lost. **Phase 2 (pattern analysis)**: same flex-child shrink gotcha that requires `min-height:0` on any flex child with `overflow:auto` to actually engage scrolling. **Phase 3 (hypothesis)**: add `min-height:0` + `overflow:hidden` to `.tb3-picker` (allow grid item to shrink to its grid cell + clip overflow at the picker boundary), and `min-height:0` to `#tb3-picker-list` (allow the flex child to shrink below content size so its own `overflow-y:auto` engages). **Phase 4 (fix + verify)**: 2-property CSS edit in `features/topology-builder-v3.css`. Pre-fix live values via preview: `picker.clientHeight=2203` / `list.clientHeight=2093 scrollHeight=2093` (no overflow). Post-fix live values: `picker.clientHeight=1051` (now matches grid-cell height) / `list.clientHeight=941 scrollHeight=2163` (overflow exists, scroll engages). Scroll-to-bottom test confirmed: previously-cut Wireless + Security + VLAN sections all reachable; bottom row `l3-switch-svi` visible after `list.scrollTop = list.scrollHeight`. `TB3_CSS_REV` bumped `r6 → r7` for dev cache-bust. **Tests**: UAT **6500/6500 ALL PASS** (unchanged — no behavioural asserts, this is pure CSS height-chain). Playwright **chromium 17/17 TB v3 tests PASS** — test 17 (`picker renders all 25 scenarios`) uses `toHaveCount(25)` on DOM elements that exist regardless of viewport-visibility, so it passes both pre- and post-fix; the v5.9.0 visual bug sat below `toHaveCount`'s detection. **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (+8 lines incl. 2 explanatory comments) · `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (1-char `TB3_CSS_REV` bump). **Lesson (locked)**: any CSS Grid OR Flex item that contains a scrolling subtree MUST set `min-height: 0` to allow shrinking below content size, otherwise `overflow:auto` on a descendant never engages — the descendant just grows the parent past its grid cell. Pair with `overflow:hidden` on the constraining ancestor to clip cleanly. Follow-up: add a Playwright visual-scroll assertion to test 17 (e.g. `bottom scenario row reachable after scroll`) so future scroll regressions are caught automatically. **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (CSS-only hotfix; no DB/auth/money; sw.js = universal CACHE_NAME bump from bump-version.js). |
| v5.9.0 | **TB v3 Phase 2.x — full scenarios catalog (8 → 25)** — hits the spec §9 ceiling. Pure additive data ship: 17 new scenarios across 7 categories, no new architecture, no new pure functions, no new UI, no CSS changes (no `TB3_CSS_REV` bump). Phase 2 surface (picker + intent chip + completion pill + backup-restore + click-drag pan + auto-close) ships unchanged from v5.8.1. **Catalog distribution (locked from manifest)**: topology 4 (added ring + point-to-point), architecture 4 (added spine-leaf-fabric + collapsed-core + soho-network), wan 4 (added mpls-wan + partial-mesh-wan + dual-isp-failover), cloud 4 (added public-cloud-only + multi-cloud + direct-connect-private-link), wireless 3 (added wireless-mesh + wireless-bridge-p2p), security 4 (added zero-trust-segmented + bastion-jump-host + nac-802-1x), vlan 2 (added l3-switch-svi). Every category has 2-4 scenarios now — the picker reads as a real curated catalog instead of "8 starter samples". **Authoring discipline**: each scenario follows the v5.8.0 concise template verbatim — `brief` (1 paragraph naming the trade-off + exam takeaway) + 5-section `examRelevance` (1 sentence each, fifth field ends with an N10-009 objective number) + `completion` block matching the starting state. Stop-slop discipline applied to the prose (no em-dash overuse, no inflated symbolism, no vague attributions, no rule-of-three slop). Device-type vocabulary held constant — every scenario uses only the 13 types in `TB_V3_DEVICE_TYPES` (`router`, `switch`, `l3-switch`, `firewall`, `vpn`, `cloud`, `internet`, `wlc`, `ap`, `smartphone`, `laptop`, `server`, `workstation`). Device IDs prefixed `sc_<slug>_<n>` per the convention so cross-scenario duplicate loads can never collide. All 25 scenarios pass `validateScenarioShape`; zero cable-id mismatches; positioning uses the comfortable centre band (x: 200-1000, y: 100-720, all multiples of 40 for grid snap). **N10-009 objective coverage**: 1.2 (topology shapes) ×4 · 1.6 (architecture + WAN models) ×7 · 1.8 (cloud deployment models) ×4 · 2.1 (switching) ×2 · 2.3 (VLANs) ×2 · 2.4 (wireless) ×3 · 4.1 (security architecture) ×4 — every Domain 1 + Domain 4 objective in the topology family is represented, plus the Domain 2 implementation surfaces that map onto curated topologies. **Architecture comparisons baked in** (the prose explicitly invokes contrasts): spine-leaf vs 3-tier vs collapsed-core · mpls vs hub-spoke vs full-mesh vs partial-mesh · hybrid vs public-only vs multi-cloud vs Direct-Connect · router-on-stick vs L3-switch-SVI · controller-WLC vs mesh vs P2P-bridge · DMZ vs zero-trust vs bastion vs NAC. Every scenario brief names the alternative shapes so the picker doubles as an N10-009 study aid. **Tests**: zero new UAT asserts (the Stage 8.1 structural guard already uses `>= 8` and passes at 25). One Playwright test update — test 17 count `8 → 25` and rename "picker renders all 8" → "picker renders all 25". All other Phase 2 Playwright tests pass byte-identical. **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (+652 LOC of scenario data only, no new functions) · `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (2-line test update) · `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-20-tb-v3-phase2x.md` (NEW, 123-line manifest with locked category split + per-scenario specs). UAT **6500/6500 ALL PASS** (unchanged — pure data, no behavioural surface). Playwright **chromium 125/125 PASS** (incl. updated test 17). tech-debt clean. **Process**: 3-way shape-decision lock (AskUserQuestion — target 25 / concise template / one big ship) → manifest plan doc → per-category inline authoring with verify-then-commit gate at each category boundary (validateScenarioShape across all entries + cable-id resolution + braces + UAT) → live Claude Preview verification (25 rows render in 7 grouped sections in the picker) → full chromium Playwright pre-push → v5.9.0 bump → canonical trunk push. 7 per-category commits + 1 test-count commit + 1 version-bump commit. **Phase 3 next** (separate plan): Simulate mode (ping/ARP/DHCP packet animation) + full reachability validator (the L2/L3 sim engine that turns the completion pill from "shape correct" into "packets actually route"). All Phase 2 + Phase 2.x surfaces serve as the canvas + UI substrate for Phase 3 — the catalog provides scenarios to validate against; the completion pill becomes the simulation verdict. **Fast-lane** per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (data-only addition; no DB/auth/money; sw.js = universal CACHE_NAME bump from bump-version.js). The picker is now a real cert-prep catalog — every N10-009 topology archetype a student needs to recognise lives one row away. |

| v5.7.0 | **Topology Builder v3 — Phase 1 canvas foundation** — full ground-up rebuild of the Topology Builder, the cert-app's flagship drill. Founder directive: "use superpowers brainstorm skill to help brainstorm the revamp… not satisfied with v1 and v2… need to incrementally build this feature." V1 (~14.6K LOC in app.js) + V2 (~3.5K LOC in features/topology-builder-v2.js) both fell short on ease of use + canvas size; Phase 1 ships the editorial workspace + canvas foundation MVP — the bones onto which Phases 2–9 (Lab + Free Build + PBQ intents, Simulate/Trace/OSI/3D modes, scenarios picker, AI coach, grade engine, v1+v2 retirement) will land bite-by-bite. **Architecture**: 9th lazy-loaded feature module (`features/topology-builder-v3.js`, ~900 LOC IIFE registered on `window._certanvilFeatures['topology-builder-v3']`) + dedicated scoped CSS file (`features/topology-builder-v3.css`, 412 lines / 14,994 bytes — first feature with its own stylesheet, loaded via `_ensureCss()` link injection so the cert-app shell never pays for it on other surfaces). Module is fully self-contained: state shape (`devices[]`, `cables[]`, `viewport{x,y,zoom}`, `selectedId`, `pendingCableFrom`, `intent`), 4 pure functions (`buildDevice`/`buildCable`/`serialiseState`/`parseState` — TDD'd via vm-sandbox fixtures), canvas render loop, pan/zoom/minimap, palette, drag handlers, cable drawing, selection, Inspector, debounced save, mode bar, PNG export. **Workspace shell**: full-viewport takeover via `html:has(#page-topology-builder-v3.page.active)` hiding `#app-sidebar`+`#app-topbar`+`#sb-mobile-toggle`+`#skip-link` and `overflow:hidden` on html+body — no global chrome competes with the canvas. 44px strip header (eyebrow `NET+ · N10-009` + Fraunces `Network builder.` title + `0 devices · 0 cables` live count). Floating modebar centred with 5 modes (`Design` active + `Simulate`/`Trace`/`OSI`/`3D` locked with phase hints) + `Export` right-anchored. 3-column body (200px palette + 1fr canvas + 340px Inspector when device selected; rrail floats as a 50px pill at `top:14px right:14px` when no selection so canvas gets full width). 28px status bar (intent label + mode + saving indicator + keyboard map: `SPACE+DRAG · PAN  SCROLL · ZOOM  DEL · REMOVE`). **Canvas**: SVG-based infinite canvas with viewBox transform for pan/zoom (50%-400% range via scroll wheel + zoom buttons), 40px grid snap on device drop + drag, hold `space + drag` to pan (cursor grab/grabbing), Bezier-cable rendering between device anchor points. **Minimap** (bottom-right corner): bronze rectangle indicates viewport position + dots per device, kept proportional to canvas extent. **Palette**: 6 groups (Routers / Switches / Endpoints / Wireless / Security / Cloud), 21 devices total (full lift-and-shift from v1's device catalogue per founder direction). HTML5 drag-and-drop API drops at cursor position grid-snapped; the just-dropped device is auto-selected (Inspector opens with bronze border). **Cable drawing**: press `c` to enter cable mode (cursor changes to crosshair, status bar shows `Cable mode · click two devices`), click first device + second device to draw a bronze Bezier cable, `Esc` cancels mid-cable. **Selection + Inspector**: click any device to select (bronze border + Inspector slides in from the right with Label input + Type readonly); typing into Label updates the canvas label live and the status bar flashes `· saving` then `· saved` (debounced `_saveDraft()` via `STORAGE.TB_V3_DRAFT = 'nplus_tb_v3_draft'`); `Delete`/`Backspace` removes the device + any cables touching it; `Esc` clears the selection + closes the Inspector. **Persistence**: localStorage auto-save survives reloads — devices + cables + viewport position + zoom level restore exactly. **PNG export**: `Export` modebar button serialises the current canvas (with devices + cables, no chrome) into a 2x retina PNG and downloads as `topology-<hex>.png`. **Modes**: only `Design` is live in Phase 1 — `Simulate`/`Trace`/`OSI`/`3D` render as locked pills with one-line phase-roadmap tooltips so users know they're coming. **Sidebar entry**: relabeled in `APP_SIDEBAR_PRACTICE_NETPLUS_TAIL` so v3 is FIRST as `Network Builder`, v1 demoted to `Network Builder (v1)`, v2 demoted to `Builder V2 (legacy)`. Handler is `async () => { await _loadFeature('topology-builder-v3'); showPage('topology-builder-v3'); openTopologyBuilderV3(); }` — `showPage()` BEFORE `openTopologyBuilderV3()` is load-bearing because the `:has()` full-viewport takeover requires `.active` (caught during dogfood when my own verify-eval skipped showPage and the :has selector silently no-op'd). **CSS cache-bust** (`TB3_CSS_REV`): manual revision counter in `_ensureCss()` so the URL becomes `?v=<APP_VERSION>-<TB3_CSS_REV>` — forces SW + browser cache miss between CSS edits even when APP_VERSION hasn't moved. Bumped r1→r4 during dogfood iteration; can be retired once APP_VERSION is the canonical key. **Files**: `features/topology-builder-v3.js` (NEW) · `features/topology-builder-v3.css` (NEW) · `index.html` (+1 page div) · `app.js` (+`STORAGE.TB_V3_DRAFT` + sidebar entry + CURRENT_CERT/CERT_PACK exposure already done for v5.6.0) · `tests/uat.js` (+33 asserts: 4 vm-sandbox behavioural fixtures + 13 structural guards) · `tests/e2e/app.spec.js` (+9 Playwright DOM tests in `topology-builder-v3` describe — using `page.evaluate` to call exposed `_deleteSelected` since Playwright keydown couldn't reach the document listener reliably). UAT **6462/6462 ALL PASS** (+33 from v5.6.0 baseline 6429). Playwright **chromium 99 passed** (existing suite + 9 TB v3 tests). **Dogfood-caught regressions** (2 rounds, the locked discipline): (1) round 1 — founder screenshot showed canvas not stretching to right edge; first fix floated the rrail as an absolute pill BUT the page itself was still clamped to the global `.page { max-width: 800px }` (and the 900px tablet-portrait breakpoint at styles.css:20041) — my id-scoped rule outranked `.page` on specificity but I never explicitly reset max-width, so 560px of dead canvas space remained on a 1440px viewport (commit `0cefc4b` adds `max-width:none` + `width:auto` + `min-width:0` + `overflow:hidden` to the full-viewport-takeover block); (2) round 2 — false-positive verify: my eval harness called `openTopologyBuilderV3()` directly, skipping `showPage()`, so `.active` never landed, so `:has()` never fired, so the html+body overflow:hidden never applied, so a phantom vertical scrollbar ate 15px from the right — misled me into thinking the original fix was working when it wasn't. Re-tested with the real handler sequence (showPage → open) and confirmed canvasGapRight=0 at 1440x900. **Lesson (locked)**: full-viewport-takeover surfaces MUST explicitly reset every inheritable constraint from the global `.page` rule (max-width, margin, padding, width) — relying on specificity alone fails because the global rule defines properties the id-scoped rule doesn't touch. AND: any verify-eval that drives a feature module's entry path MUST replicate the real handler sequence verbatim (showPage + open), not just call the feature's open function — `:has()` selectors that depend on `.active` will silently no-op otherwise. **Process**: brainstorming (3 design sections approved + 6 open questions resolved + Sec+ explicitly out of scope, gets own future builder) → spec doc (`docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-20-tb-revamp-design.md`) → 9-phase implementation plan (`docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-20-tb-revamp.md`, ~2,460 lines — Phase 1 detailed bite-by-bite, Phases 2-9 outlined) → subagent-driven dev (Stages 0-9, ~25 commits) → live dogfood via Claude Preview → 2 founder-caught regressions fixed on branch → ship signal → v5.7.0. **Phases 2-9 deferred** (per founder direction: "each phase is independently shippable and gets its own dogfood pass… re-planned bite-by-bite after Phase 1 ships and dogfoods cleanly"): Phase 2 = Free Build intent + scenarios picker (lift-and-shift v1 scenarios) · Phase 3 = Lab intent + first 5 guided labs · Phase 4 = PBQ intent · Phase 5 = Simulate mode (L2/L3 sim engine) · Phase 6 = Trace mode (packet visualization) · Phase 7 = OSI mode (per-layer overlay) · Phase 8 = 3D mode · Phase 9 = retire v1+v2 from sidebar + delete features/topology-builder-v2 + delete v1 code from app.js (the strangler-fig payoff). Fast-lane per ENVIRONMENT_STRATEGY (HTML/CSS/JS additive — 2 new files + 1 page div + 1 STORAGE key + 1 sidebar entry; no DB/auth/money; sw.js = universal CACHE_NAME bump) → canonical trunk push, CI-gated. The Topology Builder is now an editorial full-viewport workspace that matches the rest of the forged-bronze app, with the canvas + pan/zoom/minimap + palette + cables + Inspector + auto-save + PNG export foundation ready for Phases 2-9 to layer the intent + mode systems on top. |

shape `[{id, payload, attempts, last_try, next_try, terminal}]`; LRU at cap 25 (drops oldest non-terminal first); drained ONCE per `DOMContentLoaded` with 2s delay (no `setInterval`, no SW workers — single non-blocking fetch per non-terminal entry); pure exposure, no behavior change in shell) + `meta.code` (NOT `meta.objectiveCode` — that key doesn't exist; dogfood-caught regression) so Sec+ auto-context shows `secplus-SY0-701`, never leaks netplus topics. **CSS**: 230-line block appended to `dg-system.css` scoped to `#bug-report-drawer` + `.br-toast` + `.br-sp-*` Settings rows;
